Sweet Water, Bitter Water 120

— (Zuichiao)

Amidst the scorching heat, people in the city are drinking ice-cold soda, fresh bridge water, lemon water... everyone is happy and carefree, as if they have completely suppressed a fiery summer in a piece of water, dissipating it; however, recently the newspapers have repeatedly reported floods in various places, farmlands submerged, and many displaced victims, with dry tears and hoarse throats, crying for food, watching a vast expanse of water, losing an unknown number of lives and property! The friends who are drinking sweet water in the city, how have they thought about the water in the disaster area, how bitter it is?

Local Customs

Strange Country of Abyssinia 121

— Guo Jian

The African black country of Abyssinia, ever since the conflict with the Italian Somaliland troops in the Wall Wall area last year, has seen an increasingly serious and frenzied arms buildup, without any reduction, merely adding to the good material for international current events. Those who have not been very concerned about Abyssinia in the past have also gained considerable understanding from newspaper or magazine introductions.

The ancestors of Abyssinia were originally Jews. In the past, when Jews migrated to Jordan, a portion of them got lost and mistakenly reached the Abyssinian plateau, thinking they had reached their destination, and decided to settle there permanently. Later, they interbred with Negroes, and the race gradually multiplied, eventually forming the present Abyssinian nation. In anthropological research, there may be another view, but it is quite accurate to determine that they contain the blood of the Hamitic or Semitic race and the Negro race. They have continuously conquered and eliminated alien barbarians. Now, they have a history of more than four thousand years of nation-building. King Haile Selassie can be counted as the 260th generation of monarchs.

Their national character is very strong, and they do not like people calling them "Abyssinia," but want people to call them "Ethiopia." Because "Abyssinia" can be interpreted as "a country of barbarians." From this point of view, they are much better than the Negroes and Hottentots in Africa. As for those who can receive education, except for the upper class, the general public cannot enjoy this right, so most are illiterate. The script is made up of about two hundred kinds, and the shapes of the characters are very special, making it difficult for people to understand. However, when writing diplomatic documents, they do not use English or French, and always use their own language to preserve the national essence. Their laws are based on the "Mosaic Code" and the "Christian Classics" from 1,500 years ago, compiled into a very ancient code. In fact, they mostly judge a case based on the common sense or experience of the judge, without the need for any troublesome laws.

The military accounts for 30% of the total population, or about two million people. These armed masses are all under the command of the chiefs. Among them, the elite and relatively well-trained total no more than 300,000 people. Modern weapons can only be supplied to 300,000 people. The rest simply hold swords, knives, spears, shields, and clubs. As for the so-called modern weapons, the country has a total of 700,000 rifles, 300 machine guns, 200 cannons, 10 airplanes, and 10 five-ton tanks. These weapons are supplied by European countries, and there are also many second- and third-rate goods bought from France and Italy. Even rifles that bullets cannot penetrate are often found. The performance of the weapons is not taken into account at all. Frankly speaking, their old-fashioned tactics of gun against gun and sword against sword are still deeply rooted.

When going to war, in addition to the male soldiers going to the front lines, there is also a group of women (soldiers' spouses) participating. They line up behind, carrying daily necessities, climbing mountains and crossing ridges, trekking long distances without getting tired. When they reach the front line, they camp in the rear, watching the battle situation. Some prepare to be medical teams, and some are responsible for transporting bullets and food, and contacting communications. If unfortunately their husband dies in battle, the wife commits suicide to show her loyalty; or female comrades who sympathize with each other kill each other with sharp blades to show their chastity. The world only knows that the Abyssinians are barbaric, tough, and good at fighting, but they do not know that there is such a female presence inside.

Most Abyssinians regard soldiers as an honor, so many people yearn for it. Because this idea is in their minds, it invisibly makes them fight to the death to defend against the enemy on the battlefield, no matter what, even if there is only one soldier and one bullet left. For example, if a soldier dies in battle, their wife or servant immediately picks up the weapons left by the dead and fights forward until they die. If someone disobeys military orders, surrenders to the enemy, or absconds, they are treated as prisoners of war, without forgiveness, and are executed.

The Misty Records of Royal Incense 122

— Original by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

Therefore, I replied, "That's not true! Empress Dowager, so far, this servant has never been beaten by anyone." Although I had said these words, I was still very suspicious in my heart, wondering what the Empress Dowager would say after receiving my answer.

"The situation is forcing me to impose punishment on one of our officials," she didn't seem to pay attention to my answer, as long as I said it, that was enough. Then, she spoke her mind directly, "To dismiss someone who has been in the court for a long time, and who has made some minor contributions in the past, is indeed a very unpleasant thing! However, since he has done something wrong and has been thoroughly investigated, then he must be punished; if we lightly let him go without giving him some punishment, the result will inevitably be that the governors of all provinces will take the governor of Guangdong as an example, and generally become corrupt and pervert the law. What kind of system would that be? So, according to the law, the punishment he received is really fair enough: but there is still some regret, although he should be punished, but it always feels a little uneasy for us who can only勉守法度 [barely abide by the law] to punish him! Have you ever heard people say that when a father encounters his son doing something wrong, and he has to punish him with his palm or a stick, there is always a kind of painful feeling in his heart."

What feeling? I haven't heard anyone say that!

"Ah! What is it? Can Old Buddha tell this servant?" I asked very sincerely. (382)

Little Western Paradise 123

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Seventeen: Don't Ask About a Daughter's Body and Unspeakable Pain; Competing to See the Nobleman's Face and Admire the High Moral Character

Zhiqian smiled faintly and snorted in his nose, saying: Who can know what will happen in the future? Huanhua lowered his head again to play with the teacup, unable to speak. He looked at Zhiqian's face and then said in a low voice: Once Mr. Cheng explained it, I also felt that this matter was done wrong. However, only I am sad in my heart. It is too late for me to think of a way to save him. I know that Mr. Cheng has a heart of Buddha and will definitely not think anything about him, but only pity him. At this time, Mr. Jia has probably gone out. I can go to him and see. I can ask him, does he feel happy or sad? Zhiqian said, no need to ask. As an outsider, why should I care about those idle matters. Just after saying this, he made a contemplative look and said: If you didn't mention it, I would go and talk to him, which is not impossible. Huanhua put away his sad look and smiled: Of course, I can't say that Mr. Cheng asked me to go. Saying this, he walked towards Jia Duocai's room. But when he arrived there, he saw that the door was tightly closed. Even Yueying had gone out. Just as he was about to turn around and ask the tea room, he heard Yueying cough twice in a row inside. He smiled and said: Mrs. Jia, open the door, I want to come in and talk to you. Yueying opened a crack in the door, looked out, and then let Huanhua in. Huanhua saw that there was nothing unusual in the room, only two small paper-folded toys on the table. He smiled and said: I thought you were sleeping in the room. Sitting in the room well, what are you doing with the door closed? (282)

Women's Softball Rules Determined: The Women's Outdoor Softball Rules are to be Used 125

Baseball is regarded by the world as the national sport of the United States, and many countries have also adopted it. This is because its amount of exercise is quite appropriate, and it has a great function in training the individual's thorough thinking, agile action, mutual cooperation of the group, and the virtue of sacrificing oneself. This kind of game has been introduced into our country for many years, but because the equipment is uneconomical, the game method is not suitable for the general psychology, those who learn it are few, and it is not valued by the public. Baseball originally has indoor and outdoor divisions. Because the translations in various places in our country are not unified, some call it baseball, some call it softball, some call it club ball, and some even use the name baseball. Until recent years, it has gradually become unified, and the name baseball is used for men's games, and the name softball is used for women's games, which has become a habit.

However, according to the United States, there are still several different rules for softball, which are applied in various different environments, such as Indoor Baseball Rules (Indoor Baseball Rules), Playground Baseball Rules (Playground Baseball Rules), Outdoor Baseball Rules for Girls and Women (OutdoorBaceball Rules for Girls and Women), etc., which are respectively applicable to men and women's indoor games, playground games, and those specifically for women's outdoor games. Since the Fifth National Games listed women's softball as one of the championships, the indoor softball rules were used as the designated rules, and the competition was held outdoors. Although no inconsistencies were found in the trial implementation, the rules and the suitability of the venue environment ultimately failed to achieve their full potential. In view of this, the organizing committee of this conference has been thinking about improving it, so it has been decided by the Standing Committee of the Organizing Committee to adopt the women's outdoor softball rules. This rule is specifically designed for women and is played outdoors, which can be said to be the most suitable. However, it is thought that the determination of the rules is relatively late, and in terms of equipment, I am afraid that all parties will follow the old rules. There will be sudden changes, and there will be many inconveniences in skills training. Therefore, the size of the ball park and the size of the ball have been notified to remain the same, and the new rules will be applied to the game method. Fortunately, the new and old ones have minor differences in their content, and often do not affect the overall tactics.

This rule was published by Spalding Athletic Library No.t zfR in 1935. It has now been translated into Chinese by this committee and is being rushed to print and sent to each unit as a standard as soon as possible. If you need to refer to it before receiving the translation, you are advised to find the original text for reference.

What is even more important is that the scope of women's sports is narrower than that of men's, and softball is undoubtedly a suitable and peaceful game sport. The equipment is not very expensive, and it is of great value to promote it. Therefore, I hope that all units will actively participate in this championship, and hope to promote it more in daily training.

Amateur Sports Rules 126

These amateur sports rules are formulated by the China National Sports Association and have been adopted by the Fifth and this National Games.

The Purpose of Amateur Sports

The China National Sports Association has formulated the following purposes for the amateur qualifications of Chinese athletes participating in various sports competitions, such as international and national regional, provincial, municipal, and county levels:

(1) Professional athletes in a certain sport, or those who knowingly become professional athletes, shall not participate in that sport or any other sport.

(2) Amateur athletes shall not receive monetary subsidies or rewards for the loss of their salaries when participating in athlete competitions.

Definition of Amateur Sports

Article 1: Amateur athletes participate in competitions only for the love of sports.

Article 2: An athlete who participates in any sports competition for money or other benefits, or who obtains additional benefits on the due clothing and accommodation expenses, shall become a professional athlete in any sport.

Article 3: An athlete who knowingly participates in the same team or against professional athletes without the permission of the competent senior authority shall become a professional athlete.

Article 4: All those who teach, train, or guide athletes, or engage in any physical education work, and receive salaries, are professional athletes.

Article 5: Those who knowingly become professional athletes shall never be able to restore their amateur qualifications.

Article 6: Amateur athletes shall not gamble money or be involved in gambling events in any sports competition they participate in.

Article 7: Amateur athletes shall not participate in any sports competition that strives for prizes or souvenirs that cannot be engraved with appropriate words.

Article 8: The value of the prizes obtained by amateur athletes shall not exceed one hundred local silver coins, but this rule does not apply to those specially authorized by the China National Sports Association.

Article 9: Amateur athletes shall not sell, pawn, or give away the prizes they have won. These prizes must be preserved for inspection by the China National Sports Association at any time.

Article 10: Amateur athletes shall not impersonate or use other people's names to join any competition.

Article 11: When amateur athletes go to a meeting to attend a competition or return from a sports meet, they shall not receive any money or other benefits other than the actual expenses for train, boat, and accommodation. In any case, the expenses given shall not exceed the ordinary price of a passenger seat on the train or boat, and ten yuan per day or its equivalent for food and accommodation. If the meeting provides food and accommodation, the pocket money for each person per day shall not exceed two local silver coins.

Article 12: Amateur athletes shall not accept travel expenses or any expenses for their trainers, masseurs, or relatives and friends.

Note: (The meaning of this article does not mean that the travel expenses of trainers, etc. cannot be paid, but this expense cannot be requested by the athletes or paid to the athletes.)

Article 13: Amateur athletes shall not receive direct or indirect remuneration for joining a sports association or other sports organization as a member or continuing their membership qualifications.

Article 14: Amateur athletes shall issue receipts separately for any money received. These receipts shall be properly preserved for delivery to the China National Sports Association for inspection at any time.

Article 15: An athlete who sells sports equipment shall not be regarded as a professional athlete.

Article 16: Amateur athletes shall not receive remuneration for using the products of a certain company, factory, or dealer, nor shall they be allowed to use their names for advertising, or endorse the products of a certain company or factory for remuneration.

Article 17: Amateur athletes shall not use their photos for store advertisements.

Article 18: An athlete who unknowingly becomes a professional athlete may restore his amateur qualifications after being suspended from competition for one year.

Article 19: An athlete who makes false reports about his qualifications, abilities, and results, etc. shall lose his amateur qualifications.

Article 20: Amateur competitions shall not be promoted for personal gain.

Article 21: Amateur athletes shall not serve as newspaper reporters and receive money in any sports competition (or part of a competition) they participate in.

Article 22: When going abroad to compete, amateur athletes may, with the special permission of the China National Sports Association, receive money for the cost of purchasing clothing or other personal items.

The Competition Unit Singapore is Changed to Malaya 127

The Preparatory Committee of the Third Malayan Overseas Chinese Games sent a letter requesting that the competition unit Singapore be changed to Malaya. The original letter said, "This is to inform you that the Preparatory Committee of the Third Malayan Overseas Chinese Games held a representative meeting in Penang on June 29th and 3rd. A proposal was made at the meeting, stating that the competition rules of the Sixth National Games, Chapter 2, Competition, Unit Ding, Overseas Chinese groups, only lists Singapore, and there is no word Malaya. A letter should be sent to the National Games Committee, requesting that the word "Singapore" be changed to "Malaya." The case has been approved as discussed. Accordingly, we should report the situation. Malaya contains twelve districts, and the Malayan Overseas Chinese Games are held every two years, while Singapore is one of the districts of Malaya. Now your association's regulations only list Singapore, which cannot include the whole of Malaya. We ask you to approve our request and amend it accordingly, and we hope to receive a reply." This case has been approved by the 8th Standing Committee of this association, and the three words "Singapore" in the competition unit have been changed to "Malaya."

Attention to Tennis Players 140

This late summer and early autumn is the most suitable time for practicing tennis. Therefore, the demand for tennis books is extremely high. Here is a brief overview of each book: (1) "Tennis Training Method" by Made Tai, the book has ten chapters, and gives detailed guidance on the key points, attitudes, and training of gripping, hitting, and competition. It is a must-read for beginners. The price is five jiao per book. (2) "Tennis Essentials" by Bai Lang, translated by Wu Nongwei. The book is divided into twenty-two chapters and gives detailed descriptions of gripping, hitting, footwork and movements, counterattacks, returns, low balls and close balls, hitting time, serving, smashing, center of gravity movement, air balls, returning high balls, side shots, volleys, positions, and angles. This is a must-read book for those seeking to deepen their understanding of tennis. The price is seventy cents per book. Shanghai Social Education Society Plans to Promote Alley Education, First Designating One or Two Alleys as Experimental Areas, Implementing Education Methods Based on the Environment of Each Place 149

Since its establishment, the Shanghai Social Education Society has achieved great success in promoting social education and researching social education academics. The society was originally located in the Municipal Public Education Hall on Wenmiao Road. Now, due to the expansion of social affairs, the original buildings are insufficient. Therefore, it was approved by the Municipal Education Bureau to allocate two buildings at No. 8 Banfang Road near Penglai Road, and it will move to the office from today. The Shanghai Press reporter interviewed Mr. Ding Shoutang, the director and head of the general affairs group of the society, yesterday, who told us about the latest progress of the society's work, as follows:

Promoting Alley Education

The society recognizes that the environment of this city is complex, and all social situations are very different from those of other provinces and cities, especially the alleys. Therefore, it plans to use these residential alleys to promote alley education, treating the alleys as natural social schools and providing appropriate guidance based on the composition of the residents. For example, during the summer, when the general public is cooling off, this time can be used to promote education. Also, in places where dirt and dust accumulate, where feces and garbage are often dumped at will, guidance on hygiene knowledge can be given to the people. It is now planned to first use Wenyuanfang on Wenmiao Road in the South City and Banfang Road near Penglai Road as experimental areas. After it has been done successfully, it will be promoted throughout the city. This plan is largely in place and will soon be implemented.

Improving Comic Strips

Popular reading materials are the source of knowledge for the public. Comic strips are especially close to the reading materials of children and illiterate people. However, the comic strips popular on the market are either obscene and unbearable, or full of feudal ideas, which greatly affect the evolution of the nation. The society is aware of this, so it has specially compiled "Sister Wang's" comic strip, which has been published. The content is literacy education material, which is most suitable for literacy school students as supplementary material. It is said that the price is six jiao, and social education institutions and literacy schools will be given a 50% discount. The second type, "Li Amao," has been written by Mr. Xu Zhuodai, a director of the society and a famous comedian, and illustrated by Mr. Zhang Meisun, and will be printed soon.

Assisting Literacy Education

The government of this city is promoting large-scale literacy education this time. The society recognizes that literacy education is the foundation of social education, and in strict accordance with the consensus of the Literacy Education Committee of this city, the work of literacy education in the Yinxiang District of this city is completely undertaken by the society, and Mr. Lu Hailan, the director of the research group of the society, is the director of the district. The first phase of literacy schools has been temporarily established in two schools because the district is rural, and they have been teaching for more than a month.

Establishing Remedial Schools

In order to improve the knowledge and skills of adult illiterate women, so that they can adapt to social life, the society has established a women's remedial school, located near Banfang Road on Penglai Road. Registration can be made at the Municipal Public Education Hall on Wenmiao Road and the Municipal Zoo from today. The school will open on September 1.

Cultural Lecture News

The society previously held cultural lectures to revive the national culture movement. The first phase invited the famous scholar Dr. Jiang Kanghu to speak on Confucius' philosophy of life, which was very popular with the audience. Later, because Jiang left Shanghai, it was temporarily suspended. There are already hundreds of thousands of words of lecture notes, which have greatly elaborated on Confucius' philosophy of life. It is now heard that the lecture notes of the two chapters "Zi Yue" and "Cong Zheng" in the "Analects" will be published by the society after being personally sorted out by Jiang.

Little Man (6) 151

—Original by Ms. Olcott of the United States, translated by Zheng Xiaocang (Zonghai)

"These are Pompeo's slippers; but he never remembers to put them on when he comes back to the house from outside; so he doesn't get them. They are a little too big; isn't that even better? Because this way you won't run fast and can't escape."

"I don't want to escape either, madam," Ned said, opening his dirty little hands before the lovely firelight, sighing at the sudden attainment of this state.

"That's good! Now I'm going to dry you out well, and I'm going to try to get rid of that cough of yours. How long have you been coughing, dear?" asked Mrs. Pei, as she searched her large needlework basket for a piece of flannel.

"All winter. I had a cold once, and then it just never seemed to get better."

"No wonder, living in that damp cellar, with hardly a rag on his back!" Mrs. Pei said in a low voice to her husband, who was examining the boy with an experienced eye, paying particular attention to the emaciated temples, the dry lips, the husky voice, and a series of frequent heavy coughs, which shook the curved shoulders of the patched vest he was wearing.

After Mr. and Mrs. Pei had exchanged telegraphic glances, he said, "Robert, my little helper, run quickly over to Nancy and tell her to give you that bottle of cough medicine and ointment."

Ned's face showed some worry at the mention of medicine, but his fear was dispelled in a fit of laughter as Mrs. Pei made a funny face and whispered to him:

"Listen to my sly Tandy make believe he's coughing. The syrup I give you has honey in it, and he wants some too."

Yesterday morning, in addition to the local Yangtze River merchants purchasing, new merchants from Beiyang and Xiamen also started purchasing. Nanjing also made inquiries. Total transactions throughout the day again exceeded 10,000 bags. The sudden increase in purchases from Xiamen merchants, who had not inquired for a long time, was even more exciting. As a result, prices surged by 0.4 cents in the morning and continued to rise by 0.05 cents in the afternoon. Customer digestion was very active, and the future trend is still bullish. Throughout the day, 8,650 bags of Saigon rice, 3,500 bags of Min rice, over 1,000 bags of Xiaojiao rice, and 2,000 bags of Siamese rice, Guimai rice, Sukengdi rice, etc. were opened. 100 bags of Wuhu Yuan rice were also opened. If customer digestion continues to be strong in the next few days, the market will further improve.

Changzhou Cowhide and New Soybeans Enter the Market 165

This year's Changzhou Lingkou cowhide and yellow soybeans have had a more abundant harvest compared to last year, and the products are also of excellent quality. A total of two batches, totaling 270 bags, arrived yesterday and the day before. The goods are dry and are yellow-mouthed small grains. 60 bags were opened the day before yesterday, and the price was 4.25 yuan, which was distributed by the local retailers. 120 bags were opened yesterday, and the price was 4.20 yuan. The market price was 0.05 yuan lower than the previous day. Over 90 bags remain unsold, because the export merchants are not active and the local retailers lack sales. There are only a few active merchants, so the market is inevitably sluggish. With the Jiangxi new soybeans having prices but no sales, the situation of aged soybean flour and cakes is tight, and the market is showing signs of stability. However, the future trend may not be long-lasting, because the new soybeans are becoming less popular and the supply may continue to arrive. The cake sales may weaken, so market sentiment is showing slight weakness.

Silk and Tea Statistics of Chinese Silk Exports in the Second Half of July 166

Free Talk

Vegetarianism 167

— Chen Zizhan

Some people believe that "Chinese food is better than foreign food," listing it as one of the advantages of Chinese culture. Naturally, for the meat-eating group, accustomed to delicacies and rich dishes, to big fish and fatty meat, whether it's Western food or Japanese cuisine, they all feel uncomfortable eating it. That is understandable. However, they have never eaten tree bark, grass roots, or Guanyin soil, nor have they eaten only coarse rice and simple vegetables every day. They don't know that, born in China, there exists another world outside their world. In this other world, Chinese food is not necessarily better than foreign food. Therefore, when discussing the advantages of Chinese culture, they regard their group's good food as one of the advantages.

Strangely enough, meat-eaters also often praise vegetarian food. It is said that when Emperor Qianlong toured the south, he ate vegetarian dishes at Tianning Temple in Changzhou and couldn't help but smile at the abbot, saying, "Vegetable food is indeed delicious, surpassing venison and bear paws by far." However, Emperor Qianlong did not become a monk because of this. Modern celebrities such as Dr. Wu Lao advocated vegetarianism for health, and Mr. Cai Yuanpei also advocated vegetarianism. But they may not have completely abandoned meat. Using vegetarian food to change one's appetite is good. Especially for those who are generally overweight and tired of oily food, eating some light vegetarian dishes feels refreshing and pleasant. Several vegetarian restaurants in Shanghai, such as Gongdelin and Jue Lin, have good business, relying on this group of people for support. But if someone told them to abstain from meat and remain vegetarian forever, I don't think they would listen.

Several months ago, Dr. Jiang Kanghu gave a lecture on the Ten Precepts for a Good Life. His precept on vegetarianism stated, "Slaughtering living beings to fill my stomach, a barbaric custom for those who lack compassion. In terms of health, there is misfortune, not fortune. Why not eat vegetarian, clean and far from poison! Biting into vegetable roots, the flavor is complete." He said, "(Meat dishes are harmful and not beneficial, and killing small lives is morally cruel. Vegetarianism is both healthy and frugal. But specialized vegetarianism is also very inconvenient. It may be altered at any time. I hope all audience members will be determined," etc. I do not oppose Dr. Jiang's theory of vegetarianism. Even meat-eaters may promote vegetarianism. Moreover, Dr. Jiang's meaning is that vegetarianism does not preclude eating meat and can be altered at any time. Saying that vegetarianism is healthy may be reasonable because rural people rarely eat meat throughout the year, yet their bodies are quite healthy. Saying that vegetarianism is frugal is not entirely true. For example, the vegetarian food at Gongdelin in Shanghai is not necessarily more reasonably priced than the Cantonese cuisine at Dasanyuan, the Sichuan cuisine at Taolechun, or the Beijing cuisine at Zhimeilou. As for saying that vegetarianism is charitable, Buddhist abstaining from killing is the original intention. However, our so-called great philanthropists and great lay Buddhists only do good deeds and believe in Buddhism after they have money. We have not accumulated wicked money, so eating vegetarian and worshiping Buddha are not urgent matters. If there is indeed heaven and hell, we also hope to ascend to heaven, but hell is not necessarily designed solely for us. Whether or not to eat vegetarian, whether or not vegetarianism is a virtue, are not issues we need to pay attention to. Moreover, relying on only a few occasional vegetarian meals, wanting to cultivate blessings for the next life after committing sins all one's life, even if Buddha is powerful, may not be effective.

Of course, we know that the theory of seeking blessings through vegetarianism came to China with Buddhism. People in the Six Dynasties period believed in Buddhism the most, but those who believed in Buddhism and ate vegetarian did not necessarily receive blessings. Emperor Wu of Liang is a good example. This emperor, for the sake of worshiping Buddha, not only endured hardship and ate vegetarian himself, unwilling to harm living beings, but also ordered the imperial physicians not to use living creatures as medicine. He also prohibited weaving patterns of immortal birds and beasts, believing that using them for underwear tailoring was contrary to benevolence and forgiveness. Even for grand ceremonies of worshiping heaven, earth, and ancestral temples, which required livestock, he only used those made of flour instead. He was considered devout in his belief in Buddhism, performing good deeds and abstaining from killing. Unfortunately, the Buddhas and Bodhisattvas were useless, and he still starved to death in Hao City.

Perhaps it was because Emperor Wu of Liang had used sacrificial offerings made of flour that later, some people used flour-made pig trotters and lamb shanks as vegetarian delicacies. Even today, vegetarian restaurants still have names such as vegetarian chicken, vegetarian duck, vegetarian ham, and vegetarian meat floss. I remember Mencius saying, "Confucius said, 'He who first made burial figures, will he have no posterity? For he made images of men and used them.'" I think that the person who first created vegetarian meat should also have no posterity because he imitated bloody things to make food, showing that the desire to eat meat had not been forgotten. It would be better to eat meat frankly. The Sixth Patriarch of Zen Buddhism's saying that "the mouth eats meat, but the heart has no meat" seems quite reasonable. According to Wang Dang's "Tang Yulin," the first person to create vegetarian meat was Cui Anqian of the Tang Dynasty. It is said that "Cui Shilang Anqian revered Buddhism and abstained from meat and blood... When he was stationed in Xichuan for three years, he mostly ate vegetables. He hosted banquets for officials using flour and konjac, dyed with colors, to imitate pig shoulders, lamb shanks, and roasted meats, all very lifelike." This meat-eating official, for the sake of revering Buddhism, reluctantly ate vegetarian, but still could not forget his passion for meat, so he had to use flour and konjac to make vegetarian meat. It was a stroke of genius. If one used lewd desire as an analogy, vegetarian meat would be like mental masturbation, which is quite apt, but it profanes the words "vegetarian" and should be considered a sin. In short, for all those who are devout vegetarians, whether their motive is to abstain from killing, for health, or to save money, I treat them all the same and do not necessarily belittle them. Although we know that vegetarians cannot avoid eating plant-based foods, cannot avoid drinking water containing many microbes, and that not harming living beings is impossible, they naturally have their reasons for being able to go to extremes and not eat meat, and I do not necessarily refute them. As for those who use vegetarianism to worship Buddha and cover up the sins of eating meat, or to deceive for the name of a great philanthropist or great lay Buddhist, that is another matter.

Seaside of Lion City 168

— Fei'er

In Singapore, I often stroll along the coast. I love the sea. I love the surging waves, and I love the violent and majestic roar. I love the deep blue color, and I especially love the snow-white silver flowers created by the wind and waves.

In the morning, when the tropical sun first reveals its face, the Singapore coast is completely silent. The sea borrows the dawn from the east, shining golden snakes on the deep blue water. The eastern sea cape is a lush green forest, with red patches affixed to the corners of the white buildings along the shore. The sea breeze blows cool in the morning, and the wooden boats echo with the sound of "kuai nai." The boatmen laugh in the quiet morning, and their strong bare arms support the entire space. The whistle pierces the sky, and its sharp call awakens the dreams of the sinful city.

Most memorable is a foggy morning. I stood on the tip of the cape where the Singapore River empties. Watching the fog obscure the world, the sea roared with a dramatic grand tune in the strong wind. The sunlight was surrounded by the fog layer, and the golden threads turned dim. The lonely silence seemed isolated from the world, and the sound of the wooden boat's "kuai nai" could only be heard faintly. At that time, the world was like a desert island, and even the sensitive soul would sink into the dark abyss of fantasy. A kind of illusion could be heard as the sound of artillery fire, and the sea's raging waves could be thought of as mighty war drums. The boundless realm seemed to be nothingness, and the fog seemed to be a smokescreen. Thoughts would rise and fall like the tides, and all the injustices and angers of the human world would surge like the raging waves. The body seemed to assimilate into the space and time of Tao, and the sea seemed to swallow my life.

At night, the Singapore coast is filled with shadows, and the soft, green grass is filled with wanderers from foreign lands. The tide incessantly beats against the stone shore, and the long breakwater in the sea lies far away as a long black shadow. The night wind incessantly blows around the body, but beside the European War Memorial, one can occasionally hear a faint sigh. Qiu and I often sit on the stone fence, letting our feet hang down towards the sea. The sea breeze blows away Qiu's gray tears, and the sea swells up the young man's bright red blood. Every night, the sea's waves beat in Qiu's heroic heart, sending him straight to the battlefield. The sea changed the fragile outlook on life, and the sea often made people's passions boil.

On a moonlit night, the moon's silver light sprinkles on the sea. Snow-white waves jump and dance wildly in the lights of the ships everywhere. The sea washes away the wounds of the human world, and the moonlight stretches out its hand longingly to comfort the human world. The licentious music of the Raffles Hotel is hateful, but the boatmen's songs are lovable. The sea's raging waves eliminate the booming sound of cars on the shore, and only the line of light and shadow of a small steamboat, moving forward and disappearing, will attract attention.

On the coast of Lion City, the sea swelled my imagination, and the sea strengthened my will; the sea erased the wounds of my friends, and the sea eliminated the nightmares of the vagrants.

I love the sea. I love the coast of Lion City.

Our River Embankment Has Collapsed (Part 1) 169

— Hei Ying

"We common people," a young man with broad shoulders and thick lips, who had fled the disaster and arrived here, began to tell his story not long after sitting down. "There is truly a disaster every year."

The listeners remained silent. The night sky was adorned with twinkling stars, and the weather was so stifling that it was almost impossible to breathe. Sweat streamed down the storyteller's head, making his head look as if it had just been lifted out of a pool, dripping wet. Everyone was bare-chested, except for the consumptive who was wearing a blue gown and crouching in the street corner, smoking a Ma Zhanshan brand cigarette, hiding himself without making a sound. A woman called "Sister-in-law" shamelessly exposed her already not-so-full breasts, feeding her third child; while hugging the child tightly, she was calculating that there were two more mouths to feed in the family, and she felt a pang of pain, like a whip of life lashing at her heart. Some other people, however, were somewhat curious, so they urged him: "Hey, why don't you continue?"

The broad-shouldered man shifted a bit, looked at his wife inside the thatched hut with dull eyes. She was doing kitchen work for his sister-in-law. As if some accumulated resentment was blocking his chest, although his eloquence was not very good, he told people about the suffering he had suffered.

He said, "Last year, our village experienced a drought. Damn it, the fields were all dried up and cracked open, facing the blue sky, without wind or rain, making it difficult for everyone to draw water. With little water and many fields, we often had to argue with others, or else you simply had to wait to starve to death. The big scar on my ear was injured in a fight with Old Ba from the neighboring village at that time; I remember I broke his leg with a carrying pole..." Speaking of this, he spat a mouthful of saliva on the cinder ground, and wiped his lips with his hand. People actually wanted to hear the story of the flood in his hometown, but the speaker dragged on about last year for a while before returning to the topic.

"This year, the flood came!" He continued, becoming gradually excited. "In the spring, it rained a lot in a row, and everyone was worried that the river would rise; so Huang Taiye in the village came out to repair the embankment: each household was assigned to pay for the embankment repair and labor. We naturally knew the importance of the embankment, and if it wasn't done properly, a flood would be no joke, so we were all willing to put in the effort! Although the amount was a bit unaffordable. After a few days, it was my turn to go to the embankment to work, and I brought my hoe there early in the morning. That day was an overcast day, with dark clouds covering the sky, without a ray of sunshine. The river water rolled up waves with the wind. I stood there and watched for a while, and I felt that water was a truly terrifying thing. While I was in a daze, someone behind me shouted:

"Hey, are you loafing around? If you want to die—"

I turned my neck, and it turned out to be some engineer, Huang Taiye's son-in-law, standing there with his hands on his hips, with a pipe in his mouth. I jumped down and started using the hoe to send the mud to the embankment.

Temptation of Life 170

— Shen Chunhong

I cry softly by myself,

But there are no tears, only

The bitterness that has fallen from life.

Those who left me drifted far away,

Let them flow slowly with the sun and moon.

What warmth is there in the illusion of dreams?

The tired eyes can no longer bear to flicker,

And the temptation of life is falling, piece by piece.

Outside the Wall 171

— Zigang

As if I had met a devil, I had been sick for three or four months. For a person who lives alone outside, medicine is a burden as heavy as a thousand-foot stone. I lingered outside the door of the well-equipped hospital for a long time and finally had to leave, leaving only a deep sigh.

My own house is next to the street. Through the thin wall made of rotten mud embedded with broken bricks, I can hear all the sounds outside the wall, such as the choking cough of Lao Liu Gong, who sets up a small stall, the cry of Xiao Ling'er, who is called a wild boar by the children in some high-threshold families, and even the sound of street dogs chasing each other.

There seem to be more peddlers in Beijing than anywhere else. From morning till night, all kinds of carrying poles, with food and supplies, flow in the small alley like an exhibition. You don't have to go to the market or run the streets to make a living.

The vegetable carrying pole passes by more than a dozen times a day. In summer, green and purple vegetables are spread all over the baskets, and raw water drips on them. The shouts are particularly loud and complex compared to other seasons. People with only a few copper coins in their hands can also choose a few.

At this time, what people have for breakfast is sesame seed cake, fried dough twist, and white flour steamed buns. The loudest shouts are "Almond tea is ready... Tofu soy milk..." A small newspaper, as big as a palm, is also on the market. Some tearing sound is pulled out from the hard-stretched throat. You can close your eyes and imagine how small the child is. People who have been sick for a long time will hate this complicated human affair, so they are unwilling to buy even the newspaper. But every time they hear those small throats shouting, they are always moved.

Until the sun climbs into the bed, the sound of wheels rolling also increases. Cars in the nearby big alley also pass through this small alley. If it is after a heavy rain, the sound of the big leather belt slipping through the pond is so clear. Occasionally, there are still horse-drawn carriages that have not been completely eliminated, trotting by. At the corner, with a whip, the hoof sounds slow down again. Stroking my frequently throbbing heart, I know that the person sitting in the carriage is either a fat, bald old man or a heavily made-up young woman, with silk padded behind the drooping hair bun - these authentic locals. On days when my head is too heavy to get up, I lie down comfortably and use all my energy to listen to those sounds, guess, analyze, and evoke many different shadows in my heart. These shadows accompany me, driving away a little pain and a little loneliness...

The shouts of "Fatty oil chicken..." and "Smoked fish..." can make me vomit. My suffocating chest rejects these greasy things. Only when the white pear carrying pole comes, I am happy to support the door frame to explore. Some women who are chatting in the shade of the tree outside the door stop their voices and stare at me, the sick ghost. Fearing being laughed at for this incorrigible craving, I gently close the door.

In the evening, the Zhuozhou man who pushes a small cart to sell cloth always comes twice, beating the small drum in his hand. He wants to stand in front of these houses for half an hour. I can hear the nimble arguments of the several braided girls across the street: some say that the printed cloth from the day before yesterday faded when washed, and some want to measure the cloth with their own ruler.

When the stars are about to come out, the fried meatballs and fried tofu for dinner come to linger again, and the snack carrying poles slowly become sparse. The small alley seems to be quiet only for these few hours. People return to their nests like tired birds.

In sickness, the spirit at night is always so excited. In sleepless nights, I stare blankly at the window lattice. Often, I am frightened by the footsteps of a familiar madman, who always sings Beijing opera. In the quiet night, the sound of his large strides seems to trample on my heart, giving me the last disturbance of the day.

College Days (38) 172

— Written by German Storm, Translated by Chen Yinzhi

She was not among those dancing people. As I passed through the crowd of people who were dancing the waltz, I saw her standing by a window, listlessly staring at the chaotic crowd. Her face was as pale as the white rose on her head.

"Do you still recognize me?" I asked as I walked up to her.

Her face suddenly turned red. "I recognize you, I recognize you!" she said softly.

"Shall we dance together, Nali?"

She gave me her hand, lowering her head so that I could not see her eyes; but I saw how her small white teeth bit her lip deeply.

So we danced. We only danced one or two rounds, because she knew that I had not come for dancing. Soon we stood side by side under the large double doors. I could not help but look outside; it was very dark outside, only the beech trees near the house were illuminated by the lights. But a gust of flowing night wind attacked us, making people feel refreshed; I heard the music of the violin and the footsteps of the dancers, and also heard the dream-like rustling of the treetops in the forest outside.

Nali stood beside me without speaking, her eyes cast down to the ground. - I mustered up my courage. "How is Christopher these days?" I asked.

Her whole body trembled, and she murmured a few words, but I did not understand; now two dark red marks appeared on her pale corners of her mouth.

"If he comes here tonight," I continued, "then what will he say?"

I saw her breathing rapidly, her drooping hand convulsively grasping her clothes. "Please don't say it!" she cried softly, "Don't say it here, it can't be said here!"

"Where is it good to say it? Are you willing to listen to me, Nali?"

She looked up at me. "Outside," she said softly, "I want to go out too; we'll dance one more round and then go outside. - When I saw you in the side room, I wanted to ask you to say a few words to me."

We danced once more; then I sent her to her seat, and walked out of the small colonnade outside the door. - There was thunder in the distance: as I walked down the two steps to the open space, there was a sudden flash of lightning, allowing me to look down from between the trees and see the shimmering of the sea.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talks

The Disaster of American Automobiles Surpasses War 173

— Chen

The New York Police Department recently posted a notice, awakening pedestrians to pay attention to traffic safety. At the same time, it compared the number of deaths and injuries in the United States during the European War with the number of deaths and injuries caused by traffic accidents, saying, "During the European War, the American troops sent to Europe fought for eighteen months, with a total of 50,310 deaths and 182,674 injuries; while in the eighteen months before May 20 this year, vehicle accidents caused 51,200 deaths and 1,304,000 injuries, showing that the damage is even greater than war," and so on.

This fact deserves our attention. Because it makes us raise a serious question, is the development of science a blessing to our society, or is it harmful to people? This is not without reason. I remember last year at the British Association meeting, someone said that Edison's inventions had increased the world's wealth by 300 million pounds, but others said that these inventions had created hundreds of millions of unemployed people, plunging most people into poverty, which is the same kind of thing.

Naturally, we should affirm that the progress of science is increasing the interests of people. Riding in a car and using various electrical appliances is more pleasant than walking or riding in a small car, and more pleasant than the time without electric lights, trams, telegraphs, telephones, or power machines. The reason why these scientific inventions have caused countless disasters among humans is not in science itself, but in humans themselves. That is to say, as some people in the British Association said, although humanity's control of nature has greatly improved, we humans ourselves are extremely bad. In bustling cities, we have to walk in "roads like tiger's mouths". If you happen to block the path of a car, an Indian curses you, slaps you a few times, and unfortunately becomes a wronged soul under the wheels, the price is only a few tens or hundreds of yuan. Furthermore, various traffic safety facilities are all designed for the "lightness and comfort" of car owners, and the threat of cars to the lives of pedestrians has never been adequately addressed.

Therefore, the large number of car accident incidents seems to be a technical problem of traffic safety on the surface, but in fact, it is not just a technical problem, and it has the same nature as the harm caused by the revival of war to humanity.

Homeland in a Dream 174

— Jingyun

The accidental thought of home made my head suddenly swell, as if I had drunk too much, swaying heavily.

(Home! Where is home?)

I collapsed onto the bed, my eyes flashing with disordered lights and shadows.

I don't know why, but recently I've been afflicted with homesickness more and more often. Whenever I'm alone, especially in the quiet of the night, home appears clearly in my mind, until my head starts to burn, heavy, and hazy, until I lose consciousness and fall into a deep sleep. However, in my sleep, I often dream of returning home.

(Home, perhaps I can only return in a dream!)

Along a tributary of the North River, I sat in a small sampan, slowly being rowed by a boat girl with a bare upper body, her mouth full of betel nut. In the sampan, I watched the peach-red river water, with its glistening ripples, gently flowing away in layers. In the ripples, coconut shells and dried bananas occasionally floated, bobbing up and down like floating corpses. The lush coconut groves on both banks lay asleep in the hot sun, without a hint of life, only the creaking of the oars of the sampans shuttling back and forth on the river, the crisp sound of splashing water, and the familiar southern tune hummed from the boat girl's rosy lips, breaking the morning's solemnity.

(All these fresh, beautiful, and poetic scenes – from which I have been separated for many years – at this moment seem doubly dear to me!)

The small sampan turned a bend, passing a delta densely planted with tall mango trees. I could already see the atap house behind the tall palm trees standing on the shore. I couldn't help but feel happy, my heart blossoming. This was the home I longed for.

(Home, home is right before my eyes.)

The small sampan approached the shore. The first person I saw was Uncle Da Shun. He was still guarding that half-new, half-old grain boat with his son, but he didn't seem as energetic as before. His arms weren't as thick as they had been a few years ago, the wrinkles on his soy-sauce-colored forehead seemed deeper and more numerous, and his hair was streaked with white. This aged appearance reminded me of my brother's letter:

(After your studies reach a certain point, it's best to come back. Because our parents are eagerly waiting for your return… Now, Father is an old man with white hair…)

(Perhaps Father's old age is even more advanced than Uncle Da Shun's.) My heart dimmed as if covered with a layer of dust!

"Uncle Da Shun, how are you?" I went up and greeted him.

This greeting clearly made him feel surprised and astonished. He frowned tightly, staring at me intently.

"I'm Da Yun, Uncle Da Shun, have you forgotten?" I was a little impatient with his scrutiny and immediately said my name.

"Oh, you're Fourth Young Master. You've really grown up so much that I didn't recognize you, haha," he jumped up like a child, delighted. "Why did it take you so long to come back? Good, hurry home, 'Zuoshan' is always waiting for you… But, Fourth Young Master, business is really slow this year, alas!…" His face sank like a lead weight.

Arriving at the door of my home, it was quiet and still, like a temple in the deep mountains. Even Ah Hua, the dog who liked to sleep in the corner by the door, was nowhere to be seen. So, I quietly slipped inside, thinking: perhaps this unexpected return would make my loving parents shed tears of joy! But when I reached the living room, it was so silent that there wasn't a soul in sight. I couldn't hear my parents' happy laughter, or the singing and laughter of my younger siblings. Moreover, all the furnishings were very different from before. At the same time, there were several leaks in the walls and roof, as if they were about to collapse.

(Where is my home!)

Finally, I went to the kitchen behind the house, which was also quiet and still, the kitchen door half-closed. I walked in, and a wave of damp mildew hit me in the nose, which was quite unpleasant. In addition, all the cooking utensils were scattered and broken, as if I had walked into a deserted village after a robbery.

(Alas, is this my home? Is my home so dilapidated? I couldn't help but cry out, very sadly!)

When I woke up from my dream, I wiped away the tears welling up in my eyes, and lay on the bed, thinking sadly: "Home, can't I even return in my dreams?" My whole heart felt like it was immersed in a cold atmosphere…

Countryside at Dusk 175

— Ai Tu

The oppressive and noisy atmosphere of the city filled my head. The scorching sunlight shone on the tired bodies of people, and the fishy stench emanating from the tops of the white buildings gently floated with the summer breeze, sneaking into people's noses, making them feel strangely depressed.

"Let's wander out to the countryside! Drift like a rootless duckweed!"

So, I put on my crooked straw hat, wore my sneakers, and hummed a leisurely tune of the young, lightly, trying to absorb some fresh air in the countryside, trying to see the innocent faces of the children in the village at dusk in the velvety green grass.

In the afternoon, the white sun was still grinning like a monster in the western sky, broadly shining on the houses and forests on the earth. The iron wire fence of Hongkou Park was white, and young men and women with carefree smiles were running around busily. The sounds of laughter and splashing water from the swimming pool, the only place of entertainment in summer, floated in a pleasant tune, mixed with the wind from the south, and drifted along the Jiangwan suburban road.

As the three of us slowly ran along the solid dirt road towards Jiangwan, the afternoon sun seemed to welcome us with a smile. On both sides of the road were thickets and reeds with fresh wind blowing through them. The emerald green water was as still as a mirror, reflecting the white sun. There was no noisy sound, no terrible atmosphere like in the prosperous area of the big city. Although it was a hot summer, I did not feel the loneliness and sadness of the countryside.

When we strolled to Fudan University, it was the time when the setting sun was about to set in the west, spitting out a brilliant red glow, beautiful and lovely. At that time, with curious hearts and the air of strangers, we wandered around the 18th-century palace-style school buildings, looking at this place that contains a strong capitalist business atmosphere on the flat cinder road. We couldn't help but think of the shadow of the decline of the times, the beautiful scenery seen from under the blue and vast evening sky, and the licentious and desolate of the dark corners of the times from the faces of the young people who were not sad and covered with the rouge of the times - the distorted and terrible atmosphere tightly invaded my mind and heart.

Because we had run a lot of roads, we greedily ate a dish of noodles in a noodle shop near the school, and our stomachs swelled up. Then we crossed the small bridge, with empty hearts, slowly running as if exploring the road of life in a lonely world, our eyes staring at a vast blue sky. The blue sky really seemed to be boiling away the depression, an endless poetic painting, from east to west, from south to north, was always so gentle, like a girl with a shy face, covering the traveler's feelings - we slowly walked along the clear creek, gazing at the green plain, the millet branches and long leaves blown by the south wind, simply like some innocent girls jumping and charming.

The sunset was even gentler and lovelier. At that time, it had already hung under the treetops. Looking out from the broad square of the plain, all I saw was a light gauze with bright red sunset clouds. A blood vessel that was not round and intact came out from the thick and inverted needles of the poplar tree. It really seemed like a beautiful girl was hiding her body, shy and gentle. Yes! Lovely sunset. However, people living in the prosperous urban area get such precious evening scenery! Especially the beautiful sunset, simply cannot be compared with gold. So, we laughed loudly like children again, and the pleasant sound floated with the sound of the dense cars driving past us.

Musical, beautiful, stirring the traveler's heart. The lovely cicada sound seemed to welcome us, singing incessantly, and the swaying tune broke the loneliness of the countryside, and decorated the dusk like a poetic and active painting of elves.

The golden water and the dark blue sky have gradually turned black, the god of night has come, the countryside has gradually become hazy, and the lights in the urban area are also flickering. And we also dragged our tired legs and quickly plunged into the prosperous sleepless streets again. - Lovely summer countryside! Dusk brought so many beautiful shadows that I couldn't see through.

Works by the Famous Painter Mr. Li Yunxian 176

Parting Prophecy 177

— Shen Wu

… Who knows, is one instant of true life really not worth the many years of survival?

V. Korolenko.

Friend, when I quietly leave you, please do not follow my tracks, nor mention our past to anyone. Just treat this last farewell as some light ripples in the vast sea.

Perhaps these ripples will subside in an instant, but, in your memory, this instant will never be as quietly extinguished as our separation.

Whether strolling by the sea or climbing in the mountains, I tell you, the miracle of the difficulties between us is hidden here. Do not speculate, speculation will give you extremely painful disappointment and obscurity. If you like, you might as well pick up some shells by the sea and quietly take them back to your home. But, if you are not by the sea but in the mountains, pick up some pine cones that have fallen on the ground, and put them in a small box. Friend, treat them as jewels and treasure them very much! Do not allow a bit of wind to blow on them, nor allow a bit of rainwater to wet them, be attentive and careful: friend, how proud you should be!

However, from now on, the shells will no longer be by the sea, and the pine cones will no longer be in the mountains, they will never see the sky, and will be buried in the box forever. However, precisely in between, it lightly lurks with infinite sadness. Can you hear the string sound of this sadness from your memory?

Now, we are parting. I know that emotionally, our hearts will inevitably hide some inexplicable sadness. Perhaps you are even more in sadness, hoping for my return, which is your only comfort in loneliness. But as time flows like a waterfall, you will know that this expectation is gradually becoming a little empty, otherwise, you will definitely use speculation to compensate for your disappointment. However, the result of speculation is also the same emptiness.

I think you'd better treat it as some ripples in the sea of life, slowly wear away the strong memories, you should treat it as an instant of life that you have never experienced…

Enough, from now on, wind and rain will no longer invade the pine cones and shells in the box, and the giant mouth like a whip and a blood basin will no longer be able to whip quickly and suck our blood. – When our youth fades away, or when the old ruined tower collapses, friend, let us rekindle a bit of old passion from the ashes, and recall that instant of our true life!

Now, I quietly leave you, friend, please do not follow my tracks, nor mention our past to anyone. – Quietly waiting for the day to come to an end, we will use an instant of life to compensate for many years.

"Water Country Spring and Autumn" Location Team Trapped in Kaifeng 183

The location team of the Xin Xing Zhonghua Film Company's debut work "Water Country Spring and Autumn," led by director Bu Wancang, went to Kaifeng, Henan Province, on the 22nd of last month to shoot exterior scenes. It has been almost three weeks since then, and it could have returned in triumph around the 5th of this month, but unfortunately the weather is not good, and the work is difficult to complete as scheduled, so it is feared that it will have to be delayed for a few days. Now, Bu Wancang's letter is specially disclosed below: "... The kind assistance of the Yellow River water conservancy authorities has made our work very smooth. We worked continuously in the disaster area for five days. Although everyone was exhausted, their spirits were always very excited. Because everyone believed that if they worked like this, they would be able to return to Shanghai in three days. However, the heavens are not beautiful. On the 1st of this month, a burst of heavy rain and small rain wreaked havoc again, ravaging this human hell that had just suffered a great disaster. The rain on this day was really terrible. The sky was as dark as if it had been painted with black ink, and things three feet away could not be seen. Bursts of heavy rain poured straight down like a torrential downpour. We huddled in the hotel with great disappointment, but how anxious our hearts were! Because on this day, we wanted to use the borrowed plane to capture the majestic appearance of the Yellow River and the tragic situation in the disaster area. The next morning (that is, the 2nd), we got up early to see that the sky seemed to have the hope of clearing up, but we received a letter from the airport saying that the airport was wet and could not take off, so we had to wait another day. On the morning of the 3rd, we were able to fly into the sky, but when we looked at it, the clouds were low and not suitable for photography, so we had to give up and fly down, so we are now waiting for the weather to clear up..."

Shen Bao Architecture Weekly

Japanese Temple Architecture (Part 2) 187

— Itō Chūta (Author), Zhang Guangzheng (Translator)

The Significance of Religious Architecture

If we now interpret mankind as a combination of spirit and flesh, and apply this interpretation to architecture, we can recognize two types of architecture: spiritual architecture and physical architecture. Religious architecture belongs to the former, while non-religious architecture belongs to the latter.

That is to say, if the former can be called spiritual, then the latter can be called material; if the former is said to be of faith, the latter can be said to be practical. There is a clear distinction between the two.

In short, the object of religious architecture is the gods and Buddhas beyond humanity. The object of non-religious architecture is mankind. The spirit is immortal, and the life of the spirit is eternally unchanging. However, human life is like morning dew, and the life of the flesh changes like a revolving lantern. Therefore, the architecture of the spirit needs to be permanent, and it is necessary to have a style that gives a spiritual impression. The architecture of the flesh does not need to be permanent; it is sufficient if its appearance is in harmony with the material requirements of the building.

The Ideal of Temple Architecture

The most common Japanese shrines are those dedicated to the imperial ancestors. The Ise Grand Shrine, located above other shrines, is exceptionally grand. As for other shrines funded by the government and various shrines of lower ranks, they all follow the meaning of worshiping the immortal spirits. Therefore, their main halls always preserve the ancient style and are never arbitrarily altered.

However, people do not understand this principle, and some even believe that, for the sake of preserving the shrine permanently, it is possible to build it firmly with steel frames, iron bars, and cement. This is a fallacy. The ideal shrine must follow the architectural form from the time of the initial worship. As the saying goes, "Worship the gods as if they are present," which shows that the shrine is the palace of the spirits. A palace built of cement may not fully satisfy the gods. Moreover, some must follow the ancient style of wooden structures and thatched roofs, and this can only be said to be an arbitrary view that focuses on the flesh of the architecture and forgets the spirit of the architecture.

Recently, when the German architectural master Professor Pōrrō Schēdūn first visited the Ise Grand Shrine, he was also excited and praised its architecture for its purity, nobility, and cleanliness. He said, "This is not only the spirit of Japanese architecture, but also the spirit of world architecture." If foreigners are like this, how can we not deepen our understanding?

Generally, people often think that shrine architecture should also adapt to the times, using new and superior materials and applying modern and innovative designs. This is to regard shrines as the same as houses and government offices. I will not go into detail about these and will end here.

Exceptional Shrine Architecture

In recent years, exceptional-style shrines built with cement for the purpose of fire resistance and earthquake resistance have gradually been realized. There are unavoidable reasons and difficulties for this. For example, in the central areas of large cities, there are regulations that prohibit wooden buildings. Shrines in such areas have no choice but to be built with cement. Consequently, they have to helplessly alter the style, which is quite regrettable. It is originally unreasonable for surrounding buildings to be all built with cement, and therefore, the shrine in between must also be built with cement.

Since the surrounding buildings are all fire-resistant, even if the shrine in between unfortunately encounters a fire hazard, the neighboring buildings will not be affected or threatened. Moreover, if there is a shrine surrounded by lush forests and constructed in a pure and elegant ancient style among countless dry and tasteless cement buildings, with a heavy and oppressive atmosphere, it would be like a touch of red in a sea of green, which is so pleasant. People standing in front of the temple have their minds, polluted by worldly thoughts, cleansed for a moment. Recalling the past and reminiscing about ancient times, one cannot help but feel reverence. Therefore, I believe that in the cement enclosure of large cities, shrines should be built of wood. Moreover, it is even more unreasonable to demand that shrines embraced by lush forests in the mountains also be built with cement. Temples built with cement are simply reduced to stacks of the divine.

Some architects feel that the architecture of shrines has been the same for thousands of years and are struggling to create a new look. Moreover, there are many who are actually engaged in trying exceptional styles. This is a mistaken idea. Architects can freely exercise their creative skills in other areas.

Architectural Jargon 188

— Mei Zhenhuan

(Sixteen)

—Regarding uses on the construction site—

Menzi Board - When building houses and encountering cement columns (Cement Column), naturally, in addition to tying steel (as mentioned earlier), you need to support the formwork. For this type of formwork, ordinary two-inch by twelve-inch foreign pine material is usually used. However, this is a whole piece of material, only used on both sides of the cement column. But on the other two sides, menzi boards are used to seal the column itself. However, this type of board refers to ordinary Fujian pine or rough boards. These rough boards are called menzi boards as soon as they arrive at the construction site.

Rough Board - Rough Board (Rough Plank) is the abbreviation for one-inch by six-inch foreign pine board. In the construction site, this type of rough board is mostly used as a bottom board for mixing and pouring cement floors. Sometimes it is also used as a roof board. However, when used as a roof board, it is important to avoid the problem of warping.

Tadou - When erecting door frames, the wall body is difficult to rely on. The door frame must be nailed firmly on both ends with long pieces of two-inch by four-inch foreign pine material. This is called tadou.

Insertion Iron - Tying steel on the first step of the foundation (i.e., the bottom large material or pier, etc.) is done in the same way as working in the bottom. If you encounter a place with columns, it is best to tie it up from the root. This can save a lot of procedures in the work. However, sometimes, because of "life" violations (as mentioned earlier), you have to tie it later. In that case, it is necessary to pre-set the two-foot-long end of the column iron in advance. This type of end is called insertion iron.

Dou - The mixing method of cement, yellow sand, and gravel for mixing cement has certain rules in the construction site. Almost 1-3-6 is used for mixing the bottom and the whole floor. 1-2-4 is used for mixing large materials, columns, floor slabs, etc. The meaning of 1-3-6 is one part cement, three parts yellow sand, and six parts gravel. 1-2-4 can be deduced by analogy. However, there are also certain rules in the construction site for the quality of this 1-3-6 or 1-2-4. Because the quality of one part is a combination of one foot high and one foot wide, one part is one cubic foot. Three parts is three cubic feet. Six parts is six cubic feet. However, the amount of the size must not be randomly shoveled by the handyman with a coal shovel. Then use a prepared bucket to measure its quality. There are two common ways to make buckets. One is one cubic foot, and the other is two cubic feet. (That is, one foot high, one foot wide, and two feet long.)

Mantang - Making coal ash or cement on the ground floor is called mantang. (Note: The three words "cement" are the abbreviation for cement concrete).

Dui Ba Sun - A piece of wood that is one inch and six or seven points thick and four or five inches long. It is cut diagonally at the corners in a straight line to become a long triangle. The equipment used to support the bottom of the head to tighten it is called Dui Ba Sun.

Kaozi - If gravel is used to build five or six-story high-rise buildings on the construction site, it is considered as important as cement and yellow sand. There are many places where gravel is produced. The use of Songjiang goods is more common in construction sites. However, there is another type of gravel that is artificially beaten out. Most of them are from the Taihu Lake area. This type of gravel that is beaten out is not as good as the Songjiang goods that are machine-rolled. At the same time, because of manual beating, the gravel itself is not as uniform as the machine-rolled Songjiang goods. However, this type of artificially beaten gravel is called Kaozi.

Shidao - The work done on the construction site is mostly based on the sample. However, sometimes the work that should be done does not match the size of the sample. Borderline (details previously) things happen in the facility engineering. But since it touches a borderline, there must be a solution. This solution, inevitably depends on the foreman, contractor, modeler, and owner discussing it. In the construction site it is called Fan Shidao. As for Shidao, it means to research. (To be continued)

Shen Bao Architecture Special Issue Department

From Architectural Art to the Temples of Greece (5) 190

— Sun Zongwen

——The most glorious page in the history of world architecture——

(D) Zhi Tou "Capital" The Order has a very close relationship with Greek temples. The representative works of each period differ due to the relationship of the capital. The organization of a temple, the capital is one of its essential elements, and the name of the temple also varies depending on the number or form of the capital! From this, you can know how important the capital is to the temple! At that time, the most important capitals were three:

1. Doric Order

2. Ionic Order

3. Corinthian Order

Among the above three types of temple architecture, the most used is DoricOrder, so you can imagine how old the history and age of this capital is. As for the details of the capital, it will be discussed in a special section below, because it occupies a very important position in the temple!

(E) Step Stone The steps of Greek temples are usually three steps, but there are also two steps. The steps of the Parthenon temple are very special; the steps of this temple have three levels, one foot and eight inches high, and two feet and four inches wide. Because the steps are high and large, it is not easy to walk up; therefore, there are small steps in the middle of the large steps in front and back doors to facilitate people to walk up? This kind of temple with small steps in large steps is rare. And the width of each temple is referred to the size of the lowest step as the standard. It is also one of the important parts of the temple.

(F) Building Materials Why are there ingenious, bright, and great works of Greek temples? The reason lies in the result of using good building materials. Because architecture is a product of material as the body and design as the spirit, the material is improved due to the design, and the design is established due to the material; the two assist each other and supplement each other to achieve the perfect procedure of architecture. The so-called design is the technology of carving. If you want to seek the delicacy of carving, you must be cautious in the selection of materials.

At that time, the most widely used building material for temples was marble (Morblo), mostly used on the inner roof of the temple and the exterior of the capital. The most common use of marble is yellow marble, which is transported from Pentus Island and is called Penteric marble, which is one of the most famous building materials in the world. Because the patterns of these materials are extremely fine, and the colors are very similar to human skin color, after carving characters on them, they are particularly vivid and delicate due to the relationship of the colors, which greatly increases the beauty of the entire building. In addition, the foundation of the temple is mostly paved with whole pieces of limestone (Jine stone). And the interior of the palace is always based on the use of luminous materials; in this way, even if there are no windows around, people who enter it will not feel dark. This is one aspect of the situation of building materials.
